Summary of Manufacturing AI Transformation (AX) Trend Analysis

This analysis summarizes the key trends in manufacturing AI transformation (AX) across various industries such as semiconductors, automotive, and biotech, based on the latest industry reports.

The most prominent trend is the widespread adoption of 'AI Quality Inspection' utilizing computer vision technology. This is establishing itself as a core solution for yield improvement and quality control automation. For successful AI adoption, the integration of operational technology (OT) and information technology (IT) data from the factory floor, along with the establishment of a secure data sharing platform, are emphasized as essential prerequisites.

The scope of AI application is extending beyond simple inspection to early stages of product development, including process optimization using digital twins and design for manufacturability (DFM). Through this, clear opportunities such as increased productivity, improved yield, and enhanced workplace safety can be created.

However, many companies are struggling to scale AI enterprise-wide beyond the pilot phase, and the continuous operational management of AI models (MLOps) and demonstrating a clear ROI (Return on Investment) remain key challenges. For a successful AI transformation, beyond adopting specific technologies, an approach from the perspective of a 'Composable Platform' that supports flexible expansion and the establishment of a data governance framework are expected to be important.

DMG MORI digitalized the entire process chain across 17 sites into a cloud-based composable platform, achieving clear KPIs such as a 66.6% improvement in quality and a 60% reduction in manufacturing preparation costs; the core of this was creating standard apps for high-value areas like quality inspection, preparation, and setting, and then reusing and expanding them across different sites. They connected workers, equipment, and processes with real-time data dashboards, integrated human-in-the-loop with Azure OpenAI-based visual inspection, and improved operational availability and MTTR through self-service maintenance via digital SOPs and guided troubleshooting. Clear KPI/ROI tracking and the adoption of commercial composable platforms + cloud ensure rapid scale-out, security, and governance, marking it as a practical smart factory transformation strategy.

DMG MORI, by implementing Tulip's composable platform on Azure, digitized the entire process chain across 17 sites, and through real-time data-driven workflow optimization, achieved a 66.6% improvement in quality and a 60% reduction in manufacturing preparation costs. In manufacturing, generative AI and agents are already generating significant ROI (e.g., 78%), and amidst the trend of allocating over 50% of budgets to agents, application areas are rapidly expanding to core processes such as quality control, production planning, and supply chain/logistics. To scale beyond pilots, performance must be managed based on C-level sponsorship, cross-departmental governance, and clear KPIs like FPY (First Pass Yield), cycle time, rework rate, OEE (Overall Equipment Effectiveness), and delivery compliance rate. When selecting LLM/platforms, data privacy and security must be verified as top priorities. Prepare a pipeline connecting standard operating procedures (SOPs), process rules, and equipment data, deploy it incrementally starting with high-frequency, high-cost processes, track ROI against a baseline, and templatize successful patterns for replication across factories.

This report systematically details the impact of AI, robotics, energy, and network/sensing on productivity and job structures from a manufacturing AX perspective. This interview presents a direction for realizing integrated smart manufacturing by transitioning from EDA 1.0 to 2.0, where AI automates the design and manufacturing flow itself, combining multi-physics model acceleration, multi-objective (PPA-yield-cost) optimization, and generative layout. From a manufacturing AX perspective, first implement a three-pillar roadmap of 'immutable backup + isolated recovery, credential minimization/protection, and perimeter device hardening,' then map the report's TTPs to MITRE ATT&CK and operationalize them into EDR/SIEM/NDR detection rules and visibility requirements to quickly elevate SOC detection maturity.

This report comprehensively summarizes recent threats directly targeting the manufacturing industry (LockBit 5.0 for ESXi, exploitation of Oracle EBS zero-day, Excel XLL-based persistence, VPN device bootkits, long-term dormant breaches). In an AX environment centered around Smart Factory/ERP/Virtualization, the priorities for immediate action are: 1) ESXi/backup immutability and management network segregation, 2) Application of Oracle EBS emergency patch chains, 3) Control of XLL and PowerShell execution and strengthening of EDR behavioral detection, 4) Hardening/replacement of perimeter devices like Cisco ASA and MFA, and 5) Detection of Rclone, large-volume uploads, and Cloudflare proxy C2. Since supply chain/social engineering-based initial intrusion and credential theft are common denominators, increase resilience through email/collaboration security, least privilege/secret management, and tabletop exercises (ESXi large-scale encryption scenario).

Manufacturers must early identify and address 'AI infrastructure debt' and, in response to the proliferation of agentic AI (readiness 34% versus 83% for adoption plans), establish an implementation roadmap that includes edge-cloud hybrid architectures, network/storage bandwidth, GPU, power, and cooling capacity, data and model governance, MLOps standards, and KPIs for pilot-to-commercial transition, responsibilities, and OT security separation.

The Cisco AI Readiness Index 2025 shows that for manufacturing to consistently realize AI value, a 'readiness framework' that integrates the management of strategy, infrastructure, data, governance, talent, and culture is key. Pacesetters convert pilots into shop floor value by confirming use cases (77%) and measuring effectiveness (95%). Particularly, in preparation for the expanded adoption of agent-type AI (83%), it is important to proactively design edge-cloud, GPU/power & cooling, network & storage scalability, and security governance, and to amortize infrastructure debt early. Action points: AI portfolio for manufacturing (e.g., predictive maintenance, yield/energy optimization, material movement agents), commercialization gates based on KPI and risk criteria, MLOps/data governance standards, OT security segregation and real-time edge inference, change management, and shop floor skill upskilling. In the short term, focusing on revenue/customer experience, and in the mid-term, on cost reduction, is realistic.

Since the bottlenecks for AI expansion lie in power, semiconductors, and critical minerals, manufacturers should concurrently plan factories and data centers (via microgrids / long-term PPAs / onsite generation) and diversify procurement risks through multi-vendor strategies for GPUs and accelerators, inventory buffers, and lease/sharing models. Model selection should be based on task cost, security, and compliance, not token unit price, and internalize residency, private/edge architectures, and compliance frameworks in preparation for export controls and the fragmentation of regional data sovereignty. Furthermore, secure low-cost power and capital through partnerships with energy-rich regions such as Middle Eastern SWFs, and in response to China's mass deployment strategy and expanding defense demand, accelerate the adoption of on-site automation and agents to proactively manage global price and lead time pressures.

AI geopolitics is a strategic variable for Manufacturing AX. Power, semiconductors, and critical minerals are bottlenecks for AI proliferation, and the technological sovereignty and regulatory fragmentation of the US, China, and EU directly influence data and model selection. LLMs should be evaluated based on Cost of Task (CoT) and security/reliability rather than token cost, and export control compliance, a multi-vendor GPU strategy, and data residency must be internalized. Considering the CAPEX increasing due to permits/licenses and tariffs, combine power PPAs, onsite generation, and modular power infrastructure, and to counter China's low-cost, mass proliferation, accelerate the adoption of process, quality, and equipment maintenance agents. Opportunities for capital and energy linkages with Middle Eastern SWFs, supply chain lead-time management due to increased defense demand, and on-site workforce retraining are short-term implementation tasks.

IaC ìŠ¤ìºë‹ê³¼ ì •ì±…-ì½”ë“œë¡œ ì§€ì† ì§‘í–‰)ë¥¼ ì œì‹œí•˜ë©°, IR í”Œë ˆì´ë¶ê³¼ KPI ìš´ì˜ìœ¼ë¡œ ëª¨ë¸ ë³€ì¡°Â·ì„±ëŠ¥ ê¸‰ë³€ì—ë„ ì‹ ì† ëŒ€ì‘í•˜ë„ë¡ ê¶Œê³ í•œë‹¤. Misconfiguration, privilege abuse, and secret leakage in cloud-based AI (predictive maintenance, vision inspection, demand forecasting, scheduling) can directly lead to production suspension, quality degradation, and data/model theft. This paper proposes a 4-step security framework immediately applicable to manufacturing (1. Zero Trust/IAM Least Privilege and Secret Vault, 2. Secure Code and Model Lifecycle: Signing, SBOM, SCA/Container Scanning, and Supply Chain Security, 3. Training-Inference Network Separation, Private Endpoints, and Kubernetes RBAC, 4. IaC Scanning and Continuous Enforcement with Policy-as-Code), and recommends rapid response to model tampering or sudden performance changes through the operation of an IR playbook and KPIs.
ìš”ì•½:Summary:
í´ë¼ìš°ë“œì—ì„œ ìš´ì˜ë˜ëŠ” AI íŒŒì´í”„ë¼ì¸ì˜ ë³´ì•ˆ ì˜¤ë°°ì¹˜, ë¹„ë°€ ê´€ë¦¬ ë¶€ì‹¤, ëª¨ë¸ ë¬´ê²°ì„± í›¼ì†ì´ êµ­ê°€Â·ì‚°ì—… ì „ë°˜ì— ë¯¸ì¹˜ëŠ” ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ë¥¼ ì‚¬ë¡€ì™€ í•¨ê»˜ ë¶„ì„í•˜ê³ , 4ë‹¨ê³„ í”„ë ˆì„ì›Œí¬(ë³´ì•ˆ ê¸°ë³¸ì„¤ì •, ì•ˆì „í•œ ì½”ë“œ/ëª¨ë¸ ê°œë°œ, IaC ìŠ¤ìºë‹ ìë™í™”, ì •ì±…-ì½”ë“œ ì—°ì† ì¤€ìˆ˜)ë¥¼ ì œì•ˆí•œë‹¤. ì œì¡° í˜„ì¥ì—ì„œëŠ” IAM ìµœì†Œê¶Œí•œÂ·ë¹„ë°€ ê¸ˆê³ í™”, ëª¨ë¸/ì»¨í…Œì´ë„ˆ ì„œëª…ê³¼ ê²€ì¦, í›ˆë ¨-ì¶”ë¡  ë¶„ë¦¬Â·ì‚¬ì„¤ ë„¤íŠ¸ì›Œí‚¹, Kubernetes RBAC ê°•í™”, IaCÂ·CSPMÂ·OPA ê¸°ë°˜ ìë™ ê°€ë“œë ˆì¼ì„ ë„ì…í•´ í’ˆì§ˆ/ê°€ë™ë¥  ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ë¥¼ ì¤„ì¼ ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤. ëª¨ë¸ ë³€ì¡°Â·ì„±ëŠ¥ ê¸‰ë³€ì„ í¬í•¨í•œ ì‚¬ê³  ëŒ€ì‘ í”Œë ˆì´ë¶ê³¼ KPIë¥¼ ë§ˆë ¨í•˜ë©´ ìŠ¤ë§ˆíŠ¸íŒ©í† ë¦¬ì˜ AI ì‹ ë¢°ì„±ê³¼ ë³µì›ë ¥ì„ ì‹¤ì§ˆì ìœ¼ë¡œ ë†’ì¼ ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤. This analyzes, along with examples, the risks that security misconfigurations, poor secret management, and model integrity compromises in AI pipelines operating in the cloud pose to the entire nation and industry, and proposes a four-stage framework (secure default settings, secure code/model development, automated IaC scanning, and continuous policy-as-code compliance). In manufacturing sites, quality and operating rate risks can be reduced by adopting IAM least privilege and secret vaulting, model/container signing and verification, training-inference separation and private networking, strengthened Kubernetes RBAC, and automated guardrails based on IaC, CSPM, and OPA. By preparing an incident response playbook and KPIs, including for model tampering and sudden performance changes, the AI reliability and resilience of smart factories can be substantially improved.

By integrating AI throughout the entire process of design, prototyping, and manufacturing preparation, automate design exploration through generative design and simulation-based optimization, reduce redesigns by reflecting DFM/cost constraints from the outset, reduce rework and costs through data-driven verification such as tolerance and defect prediction in the prototyping stage, and shorten lead times through NC/AM path generation and automatic review of process feasibility in manufacturing preparation. However, since AI is a tool that complements engineers, establishing a Human-in-the-Loop (HITL) verification system and defining new job roles such as model owners, data curators, and design copilot operators to establish an organizational and competency system maximizes Manufacturing AX performance.

The article proposes an approach that integrates AI across product design, prototyping, and manufacturing to reduce time and costs and accelerate design optimization. The core involves automating design exploration with generative design and simulation, reducing rework by incorporating DFM/cost constraints from the outset, lowering quality risks through tolerance and defect prediction during the prototyping phase, and reducing preparation time by automating process review and path generation in manufacturing preparation. Furthermore, since AI does not replace engineers, it emphasizes the need to define human verification loops and roles for model accountability and data management, and the necessity of developing competencies for new roles such as AI/design copilot operation.

This study proposes a method to systematically enhance the reliability of on-site AI decision-making through a triple verification system consisting of a generation-verification-decision 3-mode loop, RAG-based source verification, system/external data double-checking, and comparison of multiple model results. When applying manufacturing AX, if SOPs, FMEAs, maintenance logs, and process specifications are built into a RAG knowledge base and an automated verification pipeline linked with MES/QMS/ERP is configured, it can simultaneously improve decision-making time and provide justifications for quality, equipment, and process judgments. Furthermore, UX patterns such as encouraging verification participation by considering reliability discrepancies across different experience levels, summarization of verification results, prompt/dialogue bookmarking, usage timing guides, and user initiative control provide practical value for establishing education and governance.

The paper proposes a three-stage collaborative process of generation-verification-decision-making and a TW-AI prototype to address problems identified in the UX field (hallucination, opacity, low reliability). By integrating RAG-based source verification, external information consistency checks, and multi-model result comparisons, it sorts results by reliability to accelerate decision-making. In manufacturing, this can simultaneously enhance the reliability and speed of decision-making for quality analysis, equipment diagnosis, and process improvement through presenting evidence based on in-house data, automated verification linked to MES/QMS/ERP, and comparison of results between models. CSIR's advanced manufacturing value chain presents an end-to-end model, extending from ultrasonic powder atomization â†’ ISO17025 powder and rheology evaluation â†’ MIM/casting/large-scale metal AM (Aeroswift, 2m class, high-temperature and inert atmosphere) â†’ laser surface processing â†’ HIP (207 MPa, 1400Â°C, high quench) â†’ NDE (phased array ultrasonic, microfocus X-ray) â†’ mechanical testing, which can be directly utilized for establishing standard process routes and certification strategies for aerospace-grade quality. ì œì¡° AXì—ëŠ” ì¸í„°ë„· ê±°ë²„ë„ŒìŠ¤ì˜ êµí›ˆì„ ì ìš©í•´ ë©€í‹°ë²¤ë”Â·ë©€í‹°í´ë¼ìš°ë“œì™€ ì˜¤í”ˆ í‘œì¤€(OPC UA/MQTT/ISA-95), ë°ì´í„° í¬í„°ë¹Œë¦¬í‹° APIë¡œ í”Œë«í¼ ì˜ì¡´ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ë¥¼ ë‚®ì¶”ê³ , ê·œì œì™€ ìê°€ ê±°ë²„ë„ŒìŠ¤ë¥¼ ë³‘í–‰(DPA, ê°ì‚¬ ì¶”ì , AI íˆ¬ëª…ì„± ë¡œê·¸)í•´ ë°ì´í„° ì£¼ê¶Œê³¼ ì±…ì„ì„±ì„ ê°•í™”í•˜ë¼. ì‘ì—…ìÂ·ì„¤ë¹„ ë‹¨ìœ„ì˜ â€˜ë°ì´í„° í¬ë“œâ€™(Solid ê°œë… ì°¸ì¡°)ì™€ ABACë¥¼ ë„ì…í•´ ì ‘ê·¼ê¶Œ ì¤‘ì‹¬ ëª¨ë¸ì„ êµ¬ì¶•í•˜ê³ , ì§€ì—­í™”Â·ì—°í•©í•™ìŠµ ë“±ìœ¼ë¡œ êµ­ê²½ ê°„ ë°ì´í„° íë¦„ì— ëŒ€ë¹„í•˜ë˜ ë²¤ë” ì „í™˜ ë¦¬ë“œíƒ€ì„, ë‚´ë³´ë‚´ê¸° ê°€ëŠ¥í•œ API ë¹„ì¤‘, ë™ì˜/ê³„ì•½ ì»¤ë²„ë¦¬ì§€ë¥¼ KPIë¡œ ê´€ë¦¬í•˜ë¼. For Manufacturing AX, apply the lessons of Internet governance to lower platform dependency risk through multi-vendor, multi-cloud, open standards (OPC UA/MQTT/ISA-95), and data portability APIs, and strengthen data sovereignty and accountability by combining regulation and self-governance (DPA, audit trails, AI transparency logs). Introduce 'data pods' (referencing the Solid concept) at the worker and equipment unit level and ABAC to build an access-right-centric model. Prepare for cross-border data flows through localization, federated learning, etc., while managing vendor switching lead time, the proportion of exportable APIs, and consent/contract coverage as KPIs.
ìš”ì•½:Summary:
ì¸í„°ë„· ë¬¸ì œ í•´ê²°ì— ëŒ€í•œ ì„¸ ê°€ì§€ ê´€ì (í”Œë«í¼ ë¶„í• , ê·œì œÂ·ìê°€ê°œí˜, ì‚¬ìš©ì ë°ì´í„° í¬ë“œ)ì€ ì œì¡° AXì—ì„œ ë°ì´í„° ì£¼ê¶Œê³¼ ìƒí˜¸ìš´ìš©ì„±, ì±…ì„ì„± ê°•í™”ë¡œ ë²ˆì—­ë  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. ì‹¤ë¬´ì ìœ¼ë¡œëŠ” ë©€í‹°ë²¤ë”Â·ë©€í‹°í´ë¼ìš°ë“œ, ì˜¤í”ˆ í‘œì¤€ ê¸°ë°˜ í†µí•©, ë°ì´í„° í¬í„°ë¹Œë¦¬í‹°Â·ì—‘ì‹¯ ê³„íš, ê³µê¸‰ë§ ë°ì´í„° ê±°ë²„ë„ŒìŠ¤(ë¶„ë¥˜Â·êµ­ê²½ ê°„ ë§µÂ·DPAÂ·ê°ì‚¬ì¶”ì ), ì‘ì—…ì/ì„¤ë¹„ ì¤‘ì‹¬ì˜ ë™ì˜Â·ì ‘ê·¼ê¶Œ ê´€ë¦¬(ì‚°ì—…í˜• ë°ì´í„° í¬ë“œ) ë„ì…ì´ í•µì‹¬ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì§€ì—­ë³„ ê·œì œì™€ ë°ì´í„° íë¦„ ì œì•½ì— ëŒ€ë¹„í•´ ì§€ì—­í™”Â·ì—°í•©í•™ìŠµÂ·ê°€ëª…ì²˜ë¦¬ë¥¼ í¬í•¨í•œ ì„¤ê³„ë¥¼ ì¤€ë¹„í•˜ê³ , API ë‚´ë³´ë‚´ê¸° ë¹„ì¤‘Â·ë²¤ë” ì „í™˜ ë¦¬ë“œíƒ€ì„ ë“± KPIë¡œ ì‹¤í–‰ë ¥ì„ ì ê²€í•˜ëŠ” ê²ƒì´ ìœ ìš©í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. The three perspectives on solving internet problems (platform divestiture, regulation/self-reform, user data pods) can be translated into enhanced data sovereignty, interoperability, and accountability in manufacturing AX. Practically, the key is the adoption of multi-vendor/multi-cloud, open standard-based integration, data portability/exit plans, supply chain data governance (classification, cross-border maps, DPA, audit trails), and worker/equipment-centric consent and access rights management (industrial data pods). To prepare for regional regulations and data flow restrictions, it is useful to prepare designs that include localization, federated learning, and pseudonymization, and to check implementation effectiveness with KPIs such as API export ratio and vendor switching lead time.

To respond to rare earth supply chain risks, you must quantify the usage of Nd, Pr, Dy, Tb and dependence on Chinese refining and processing at the BOM level to set priorities, and secure operational resilience through lead time and inventory simulations that assume export controls and delays in origin verification. Simultaneously, raise technological and procurement self-reliance by dual-sourcing with non-Chinese mining and refining companies like MP Materials, pursuing NdFeB reduction designs (such as SR/induction motors, ferrite, and grain boundary diffusion), and implementing magnet recovery and reprocessing. In the deployment of humanoid/mobile robots in manufacturing sites, reducing cabling and controller complexity by bundling motion, perception, and safety with edge integrated controlâ€”like the NexCOBOTâ€“NVIDIA-based 'unified control platform (MARS400 T10)'â€”decreases installation, maintenance, and redeployment costs, and facilitates practical deployment for both wheeled and bipedal types. Realistic deployment involves operating pilots from mobile + manipulation tasks in manufacturing and logistics (e.g., material transfer, picking, loading/unloading, line maintenance support), securing collaborative safety, collision avoidance, emergency stop, and certification, and concurrently managing TCO (Total Cost of Ownership) including power/battery, network, cybersecurity, and operator training.

NexCOBOT, in collaboration with NVIDIA, introduces an approach aimed at simplifying humanoid robot control architecture (MARS400 T10) and addressing safety challenges. Reduced cabling and control complexity can lower initial adoption barriers by decreasing installation/maintenance costs and risks in manufacturing and logistics sites. For manufacturers, a practical approach is to begin pilot projects with repetitive tasks such as logistics and material handling, and to evaluate them from a total cost of ownership perspective, including safety features, power/battery operation, and worker collaboration procedures.

As semiconductors, power, and critical minerals become bottlenecks due to global AI competition and geopolitical risks, manufacturers must secure stable AI infrastructure by simultaneously pursuing CapEx plans (including computing lead time and power capacity), long-term contracts for GPU/AI chips and a mix of alternative hardware (edge inference), and PPA and energy efficiency investments. Considering US-China regulations and regional digital sovereignty demands, proactively align with regulatory compliance, including export controls and the EU AI Act, alongside scenario planning that integrates multi-sourcing, production in friendly nations, and buffer inventory into S&OP. Simultaneously, productivity and quality can be enhanced by introducing high-reliability requirements such as AI Copilot-based work standards, upskilling and reskilling roadmaps, traceability, model risk management, and cybersecurity.

The core of the article is the bottleneck for AI proliferation (hardware (semiconductors), critical minerals, and electricity) and the differentiation of regional AI strategies, centered around US-China competition. Based on this, the manufacturing sector must realign its S&OP/CapEx plans, which integrate diversification of GPU/accelerator procurement, long-term power purchase agreements and energy efficiency investments, and responses to export controls along with production strategies in friendly nations. Simultaneously, by establishing a copilot-based standard work and retraining system in preparation for workforce transformation, and proactively introducing defense-level trust and security requirements, risks can be reduced while creating a competitive advantage.

The core application areas of Generative AI in manufacturing include SOP/safety procedure Q&A knowledge assistants, vision quality inspection (synthetic data augmentation), process document and work instruction automation, design-to-manufacturing transition (BOM/routing), demand/supply scenarios, and predictive maintenance ticket summarization and RCA, among others, simultaneously enhancing quality, efficiency, and innovation. Implementation begins with a 90-day document- and text-centric RAG PoC, followed by MES/PLM/ERP integration, authorization, security, and compliance (ISO 9001/IATF 16949), human-in-the-loop, KPI management (FPY, Cycle Time, MTBF/MTTR, NCR), and edge/cloud deployment decisions, then expands to include model monitoring and retraining, and CoE and on-site training/certification (e.g., GSDC). Expected outcomes include reduced repetitive documentation tasks, and decreased decision-making lead time and line downtime.
